  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cbc2200a-d9bb-4bcf-8508-845d257874b6'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11185729863365661719">How far would you go for the best friend who broke your heart? This internationally bestselling novel tells an enchanting tale of life’s most unpredictable loves and heartaches, and the unforgettable bond between a single woman and an extraordinary five-year-old girl.   <span id="freeText11185729863365661719" style="display:none">How far would you go for the best friend who broke your heart? This internationally bestselling novel tells an enchanting tale of life’s most unpredictable loves and heartaches, and the unforgettable bond between a single woman and an extraordinary five-year-old girl. From the moment they met in college, best friends Adele Brannon and Kamryn Matika thought nothing could come between them—until Adele did the unthinkable and slept with Kamryn’s fiancé, Nate. Now, after years of silence, the two women are reuniting, and Adele has a stunning request for her old friend: she wants Kamryn to adopt her five-year-old daughter, Tegan.<br /><br />Besides the difference in skin color—many will assume that headstrong, impulsive Kamryn is Tegan’s nanny—there’s the inconvenient truth that Kamryn is wholly unprepared to take care of anyone, especially someone who reminds her so much of Nate. With crises brewing at work and her love life in shambles, can Kamryn somehow become the mother a little girl needs her to be? <br /><br />In<b> My Best Friend’s Girl</b><i>,</i> Dorothy Koomson takes us on a warm and wondrous journey through laughter and tears, forgiveness and hope—and the enduring love forged by the unlikeliest of families.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11185729863365661719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2680454" />
    <a title="Maria Elmvang" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/168347-maria-elmvang"><img alt="Maria Elmvang" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442612167p2/168347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2680454?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Elmvang" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Elmvang" href="/user/show/168347-maria-elmvang">Maria Elmvang</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751537079" href="/book/show/715016.My_Best_Friend_s_Girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=2007">2007</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=owned-physical-book">owned-physical-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/168347-maria-elmvang?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2680454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14699677559822694433">"My Best Friend's Girl" was a LOT better than I'd expected it to be. I don't know why I wasn't expecting too much of it - I mean, after all I <i>bought</i> it, surely I must have felt it was worth reading? I think my problem is that I'd gotten to the point where I felt good chick-lit is hard to find, and that this one would be as shallow as the rest. Fortunately I was mistaken. I laughed and cried in turn practically from page one. It's an extremely moving story and one that has you guessing right to t</span>
  <span id="freeText14699677559822694433" style="display:none">"My Best Friend's Girl" was a LOT better than I'd expected it to be. I don't know why I wasn't expecting too much of it - I mean, after all I <i>bought</i> it, surely I must have felt it was worth reading? I think my problem is that I'd gotten to the point where I felt good chick-lit is hard to find, and that this one would be as shallow as the rest. Fortunately I was mistaken. I laughed and cried in turn practically from page one. It's an extremely moving story and one that has you guessing right to the very end. I ended up loving the characters and simply couldn't put the book down. I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14699677559822694433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14620219834857802171">3.5★<br/><br/>Kamryn Matika and Adele Brannon were best friends that was until, Adele slept with Kamryn's fiance, Nate. If that wasn't bad enough, Kamryn then finds out that, Adele is pregnant with Nate's baby. After finding out all this shocking information, Kamryn decides she wants nothing to do with either of them and it's now time to move on with her own life.<br/><br/>Two years later, Kamryn is all excited about celebrating her birthday and greets the mailman as she knows there will be a few cards for her, but</span>
  <span id="freeText14620219834857802171" style="display:none">3.5★<br /><br />Kamryn Matika and Adele Brannon were best friends that was until, Adele slept with Kamryn's fiance, Nate. If that wasn't bad enough, Kamryn then finds out that, Adele is pregnant with Nate's baby. After finding out all this shocking information, Kamryn decides she wants nothing to do with either of them and it's now time to move on with her own life.<br /><br />Two years later, Kamryn is all excited about celebrating her birthday and greets the mailman as she knows there will be a few cards for her, but her excitement soon fades when she opens one of the cards and quickly discovers it's from, Adele. But this is not just a normal birthday card because the words that are written in this card could change, Kamryn's life for ever. Adele has leukemia and is dying and knows she hasn't got much more time left, but she needs to make sure the one person in her life is taken care of and that is her five year old daughter, Tegan. Adele believes the best person to care for her daughter is, Kamryn, but Kamryn doesn't agree. Kamryn has no idea how to take of a young child and nor does she have any plans of having a child in the near future. Can Adele convince, Kamryn that she is best person to take care of her daughter?<br /><br />A heartbreaking story about friendship, grief, forgiveness and responsibility. I really enjoyed this book it was an easy read, but at times it was a little sad which could easily leave the reader feeling a bit emotional. I have no hesitation in recommending this book.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751537079" href="/book/show/715016.My_Best_Friend_s_Girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665668-charlie?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665668-charlie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665668-charlie?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665668-charlie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350733969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6621534005934891838"><blockquote>
  <b><i>"I was laughing and crying from page one."</i> - Adele Parks</b>
</blockquote><br/>This book exceeded my expectations. I fell in love with the blurb and it urged me to buy it but I never thought I could fall in love more than I already am. It was a perfect mix of a heart-warming and gut-wrenching story. I thought I knew how the story would roll and that I would just need to be filled with the little gaps in between but I was wrong. I never even guessed the ending.<br/><br/>Koomson did a perfect job in characterization because t</span>
  <span id="freeText6621534005934891838" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b><i>"I was laughing and crying from page one."</i> - Adele Parks</b>
</blockquote><br />This book exceeded my expectations. I fell in love with the blurb and it urged me to buy it but I never thought I could fall in love more than I already am. It was a perfect mix of a heart-warming and gut-wrenching story. I thought I knew how the story would roll and that I would just need to be filled with the little gaps in between but I was wrong. I never even guessed the ending.<br /><br />Koomson did a perfect job in characterization because they felt so real and tangible like they were present in the same room where I was. Their feelings and emotions felt real too. I actually have to stop every paragraph once in a while to catch my breath and calm down. I was already struggling to stop myself from crying after I've read the prologue and to think that this book has 437 pages was scary. Scary in a way that I might end up looking extremely horrible after I've read it with puffy and red eyes.<br /><br />I instantly fell in love with Tegan. She has that ability to make everyone fall in love with her without even trying. I suppose, this came from her mother and I wish we knew more of Adele but then I have to remind myself that this story is about Kamryn's journey towards acceptance, grief, forgiveness and happiness. I understand apprehension and doubts with regards to other people and herself and I understand her the whole time I was reading the book. I didn't blamed her at some parts where I thought I would.<br /><br />The boys... Luke was amazing. I never thought anyone could easily be that close and comfortable to a child but he was natural. I was wary of everything about Nate on the other hand, even though he seemed sincere when he came back. (Maybe that's just me and the sore issue about infidelity)<br /><br />As what Adele Parks said in the cover of the book, this has made me laugh and cry repeatedly since I started reading it. But no matter how much I've cried, I think it was worth the tears. This story is really amazing and touching and, did I already say amazing?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6621534005934891838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_26321589" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26321589" />
    <a title="Christa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/261662-christa"><img alt="Christa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524003029p2/261662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26321589?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christa" href="/user/show/261662-christa">Christa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/261662-christa?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26321589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12849969307363088893">About a quarter of the way through this book, I almost decided not to read the rest of it, which is very unusual for me. I was not finding any of the adult characters likeable, and was not enjoying reading about them. I decided to keep trying to go on, and before long, I finally started to empathize with the characters barely enough to care what became of them. The main character, Kamryn Matika, is given a huge shock when her estranged dying friend, Adele, asks her to raise her child. The two be</span>
  <span id="freeText12849969307363088893" style="display:none">About a quarter of the way through this book, I almost decided not to read the rest of it, which is very unusual for me. I was not finding any of the adult characters likeable, and was not enjoying reading about them. I decided to keep trying to go on, and before long, I finally started to empathize with the characters barely enough to care what became of them. The main character, Kamryn Matika, is given a huge shock when her estranged dying friend, Adele, asks her to raise her child. The two became estranged two years previously when Kamryn found out that Adele's daughter, Tegan, whom Kamryn loves, is the product of an affair between Adele and Kamryn's fiance, Nate. Kamryn broke off both relationships and moved away. After Adele dies, Kamryn does her best with Tegan, and they both become attached to Kamryn's boss, Luke. Before long, Nate comes back into the picture, and Kamryn's relationship with Luke is threatened, both by Nate and by Luke's feelings for a former fiance. <br /><br />I thought that all of the characters acted childish much of the time, and I didn't ever feel that either Kamryn or Luke were really committed to each other. I didn't mind that the characters were flawed, but the descriptions Kamryn constantly gave of herself as being unfriendly and unlikeable made it difficult for me to warm up to her. I did like the way she tried so hard to do what was right for Tegan. Luke came across as a really nice sympathetic guy most of the time, but it was hard to get past how nasty he was to Kamryn when they met, and the way he made derogatory comments about her looks and weight when they first met. The premise of this book made for a good story, but for me, the characters were a little too flawed and caught up in their pasts to be enjoyable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12849969307363088893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_725945314" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/725945314" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20608600-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601760778p2/20608600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/725945314?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/20608600-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20608600-laura?shelf=four-star">four-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer725945314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4156418572915308084">It takes a special kind of book to bring tears to your eyes - I can count on one hand the amount of books that have made me shed tears in their wake, this being one of the first.<br/><br/>Best friends Adele and Kamryn are inseperable in their formative years; until one makes the terrible decision to sleep with the others fiance. Picking up a few years later, Adele shows up at Kamryn's door begging her to adopt her little girl.<br/><br/>It is easy to see why this novel became so successful, and an international best</span>
  <span id="freeText4156418572915308084" style="display:none">It takes a special kind of book to bring tears to your eyes - I can count on one hand the amount of books that have made me shed tears in their wake, this being one of the first.<br /><br />Best friends Adele and Kamryn are inseperable in their formative years; until one makes the terrible decision to sleep with the others fiance. Picking up a few years later, Adele shows up at Kamryn's door begging her to adopt her little girl.<br /><br />It is easy to see why this novel became so successful, and an international bestseller. Despite being Koomson's third novel, this is perhaps her best work. The social issues raised in this book were gripping at times, heartbreaking during others. It is a complete rollercoaster of emotions and a real journey through deception, courage, strength and forgiveness. <br /><br />At times I felt the book to be ever so slightly tedious and a few 'scenes' felt rather irrelevent. However, I would still highly recommend this book to those seeking a different sort of chick lit. This is not a love story in terms of romance - its a different type of love, perhaps the most forgiving. Maybe we can all learn something from adopting the essence of this story. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3082571677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3082571677" />
    <a title="Denisa Arsene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43388480-denisa-arsene"><img alt="Denisa Arsene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580911704p2/43388480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3082571677?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisa Arsene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisa Arsene" href="/user/show/43388480-denisa-arsene">Denisa Arsene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789734608058" href="/book/show/16037437-fetita-prietenei-mele">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43388480-denisa-arsene?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3082571677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4446257128853528370">3,5 stars<br/>This book and its subject are really sensitive: I refer to the fact that a woman has to adopt a little girl whose mother recently died. But here, the story gets a bit tangled. The girl is the daughter of woman's best friend and her ex fiance. And this is what I didn't like: the adults seem a bit unreal, childish, ignorant, stupid even. <br/>The little girl, Tegan, or Tiga, is more mature, intelligent and real than the adults. I know all of them had traumas in their childhood, but they are gr</span>
  <span id="freeText4446257128853528370" style="display:none">3,5 stars<br />This book and its subject are really sensitive: I refer to the fact that a woman has to adopt a little girl whose mother recently died. But here, the story gets a bit tangled. The girl is the daughter of woman's best friend and her ex fiance. And this is what I didn't like: the adults seem a bit unreal, childish, ignorant, stupid even. <br />The little girl, Tegan, or Tiga, is more mature, intelligent and real than the adults. I know all of them had traumas in their childhood, but they are grownups, they could change and understand life better. I liked Luke, too. <br />Regardless, I liked the story. And I felt a lot for Tiga, even for Ryn and for Luke. Sometimes even for Nate. But I can't agree and I can't understand the treason! And this part of the story seems unrealistic. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3717907699137002623">The book starts off with an interesting premise- your ex best friend who slept with your fiancee and fathered his child is dying and wants you to adopt her child. I thought this may lead to an interesting soul searching book with her torn between the betrayal and the stark reality of the situation, but no. instead it was a weak story with no character development based in a fantasy world. first of all, Ryn decides just like that, that she will adopt the child. her friend passes away and suddenly</span>
  <span id="freeText3717907699137002623" style="display:none">The book starts off with an interesting premise- your ex best friend who slept with your fiancee and fathered his child is dying and wants you to adopt her child. I thought this may lead to an interesting soul searching book with her torn between the betrayal and the stark reality of the situation, but no. instead it was a weak story with no character development based in a fantasy world. first of all, Ryn decides just like that, that she will adopt the child. her friend passes away and suddenly she forgets the betrayal. the child is up rooted and lost her mum but somehow is completely fine with it and barely shows any signs ofgrief at all. i know kids are resilient but come on. Ryn shows some sign of grief in that she cries, but that is it. your ex bf dies and you're left with your ex fiancees child from him cheating on you, but yeah just a little cry here or there. i expected this to explore the grief and confusion together with the new life of looking after an also grieving child, but itbarely even dipped a toe. it focussed more on the stupid story of her boss who hates her, but then hangs around because he likes the kid. (weird enough that her boss hangs out with them but wierder that he does even when they hate each other) lo and behold they fall in love, her ex comes back, things get confusing then her boss marries someone else. at the end of course her boss comes back to her. clearly thought his marriage through well. no character development, no dealing of the issues, just a crap excuse for a love story, clearly written for a dramatic film of 'oh he came back.' wasted my time on this book, so much was thrown in that was never dealt with, it was just a love story parading as something better.</span>

  <span id="freeText5783257491697401101" style="display:none">One of my favorite books of all time is the timeless novel “My Best Friend’s Girl” by one of my favorite authors Dorothy Koomson. I have read it over and over as the loveliness of this books is just too overwhelming. <br /><br />I just adore this book. It is so beautifully written, so realistic, so filled with emotions you would find your self lost in the pages. It’s the kind of book you wish you could lose sleep over so you could finish… it’s the kind of book you could forsace your social life just to flip it’s pages… If you ever took your life for granted and thought that you will stay the same for the rest of eternity… if you ever had a fight with someone and cut them off your life believing you will never cross their pass again… if you ever thought forgiveness was something beyond imaginable for a fatal mistake… if you cannot imagine your self becoming responsible for another human being overnight… This is the book for you… the message is loud and clear… Never Say Never!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5642549289807551507">I had some big expectations of this book. With all the high ratings and praise it was given, I was thoroughly looking forward to this book. I expected high emotions and a great story, which is what I got. But the execution of the story itself is what disappointed me. I'll tell you why:<br/><br/>At the beginning the interaction of Ryn and Del felt genuine and I enjoyed that. All the way up to Ryn interacting with Tegan was great. But then once Luke and Nate got involved, it was just so over the place. I ju</span>
  <span id="freeText5642549289807551507" style="display:none">I had some big expectations of this book. With all the high ratings and praise it was given, I was thoroughly looking forward to this book. I expected high emotions and a great story, which is what I got. But the execution of the story itself is what disappointed me. I'll tell you why:<br /><br />At the beginning the interaction of Ryn and Del felt genuine and I enjoyed that. All the way up to Ryn interacting with Tegan was great. But then once Luke and Nate got involved, it was just so over the place. I just felt like the dynamics of Ryn and the men were just off somehow. I can't really explain it. About three quarters' into the book, I was dreading the end. And once it happened, it left me feeling incomplete about the whole story itself. I don't know if I like it enough to give it 3 whole stars, but it was still good enough that I don't regret reading it.<br /><br />It's funny how I've not felt like this about a book in a while. I guess you'll just have to read it and find out for yourself. :)</span>

<div id="review_579921409" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579921409" />
    <a title="Bookphenomena (Micky) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18967379-bookphenomena-micky"><img alt="Bookphenomena (Micky) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581468454p2/18967379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579921409?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookphenomena (Micky) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookphenomena (Micky) " href="/user/show/18967379-bookphenomena-micky">Bookphenomena (Micky) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751537079" href="/book/show/715016.My_Best_Friend_s_Girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=old-favourites">old-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579921409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16592105870938045470">I've just re-read this, having originally read it nearly 10 years ago. I had forgotten much of the detail but I can say this book was like a magnet, I couldn't look away. It is a bittersweet tale of love, grief and relationships. There are a number of sections in this book that pack such an emotional punch, that it takes your breath away and floods your eyes. Koomson has a very inviting writing style; I felt drawn in close to the characters. <br/><br/>Adele is gravely ill and needs to ensure her daughter </span>
  <span id="freeText16592105870938045470" style="display:none">I've just re-read this, having originally read it nearly 10 years ago. I had forgotten much of the detail but I can say this book was like a magnet, I couldn't look away. It is a bittersweet tale of love, grief and relationships. There are a number of sections in this book that pack such an emotional punch, that it takes your breath away and floods your eyes. Koomson has a very inviting writing style; I felt drawn in close to the characters. <br /><br />Adele is gravely ill and needs to ensure her daughter Tegan has guardianship. She hasn't spoken to her best friend Kamryn for two years. She has a big request to ask.<br /><br />The blurb is clear that tough reading is ahead but there are many unexpected twists and turns. This is the kind of read that sticks with you but I don't choose to read them all the time. Just utterly memorable. <br /><br />Reviewed for Jo&amp;IsaLoveBooks Blog.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2387149980095819278">This is a surprisingly sweet story. It looks like chicklit, and I think it certainly tried to sell itself as chicklit based on cover copy and design, but evades that genre with more sweetness and depth. <br/><br/>Honestly, I could have done without Kamryn's romantic struggles and would have preferred to see more focus on her growing relationship with Tegan, her adopted daughter. <br/><br/>The book was an overall enjoyable read, but I feel like it broke down at the end and felt false and rushed. </span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831423-leonor-sousa?shelf=owned">owned</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3357697763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16730826437554802583">I'm not and never have been a big fan of (adult) romances. If they are young-adult, dark or contemporary I do like them but those "classic" romances have never been much my genre. Nonetheless, one of my big goals is to explore all kinds of literature, so when for the first month of #tryallthereads, the chosen genre was romance, I accepted it as a challenge.<br/>I didn't had any romances on my TBR so I had to borrow the only book my mom owns and that happened to be a romance: My Best Friend's Girl, by</span>
  <span id="freeText16730826437554802583" style="display:none">I'm not and never have been a big fan of (adult) romances. If they are young-adult, dark or contemporary I do like them but those "classic" romances have never been much my genre. Nonetheless, one of my big goals is to explore all kinds of literature, so when for the first month of #tryallthereads, the chosen genre was romance, I accepted it as a challenge.<br />I didn't had any romances on my TBR so I had to borrow the only book my mom owns and that happened to be a romance: My Best Friend's Girl, by Dorothy Koomson. I started reading with no expectations and was a little bit surprised.<br />I liked the beginning of the story and loved Tegan from the start. That kid is awesome! However, I didn't like the development of the story from the point Nate showed up. I thought the main character, Kamryn was inconsistent and that really upset me. I know she had been through a lot but still... I also thought that some details were a bit unreal like the change in Luke's opinion on Kamryn. This change was also a bit predictable but since I was rooting for them, I was able to tolerate it. About the ending, I liked that it was an incognita till the end, but once again I felt like it wasn't very consistent.<br />To conclude, I had some fun reading this book but, unfortunatelly, there were some details that stopped me from giving it a better ratting</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38508628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38508628" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1714201-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226651128p2/1714201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38508628?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1714201-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38508628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8485135337804956301">I picked this up in England as a chick-lit-vacation-read. I barely scanned the back of the book before grabbing it, and somehow missed that "best friend's girl" wasn't "best friend's girlfriend" (that, one would assume, the narrative "my" was also after), but rather "best friend's daughter." And that the promised romance (because, after all, the cover was in soft pink and green pastels -- come on!) was not between these two characters.<br/><br/>Do not read this book in public. Especially if you're a woman</span>
  <span id="freeText8485135337804956301" style="display:none">I picked this up in England as a chick-lit-vacation-read. I barely scanned the back of the book before grabbing it, and somehow missed that "best friend's girl" wasn't "best friend's girlfriend" (that, one would assume, the narrative "my" was also after), but rather "best friend's daughter." And that the promised romance (because, after all, the cover was in soft pink and green pastels -- come on!) was not between these two characters.<br /><br />Do not read this book in public. Especially if you're a woman with closely-held female friendships. Very very dangerous. Here's why: the story kicks off when the main character, Ryn, receives a birthday card from one-time best friend Adele. They haven't spoken in four years for reasons best explained in the book, but Del is getting in touch now because she's dying. And Ryn is still the named legal guardian for Del's five-year-old, Tegan. <br /><br />Yes, it goes there.<br /><br />Del shuffles off the mortal coil pretty quickly, but that doesn't really lessen the emotional impact. The relationship between the two women--and Ryn's attempts to work through her rift with Del post-mortem--is the major thread in the book. Dorothy Koomson does a great job of creating a friendship that feels real, and that provides a framework for the rest of the novel. If you have girlfriends with whom you are as close as Del and Ryn are with each other, you WILL cry. There's just no way around it. I was reading this book while taking mass transit all over England, and I still cried. I cried so hard, I had to re-hydrate after reading. <br /><br />So, the run-down: great book for what it is--that is, vacation-friendly, light, reading for chicks. Know this getting into it. And be sure to bring your hankies with you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8485135337804956301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9991649914593438231" style="display:none">I hate this author..seriously, I hate this girl..because as soon as I get her book in my hands, she makes me desperately wish for a weekend...and then on Friday night, this girl keeps me awake till 4 as I try to finish this book...reach the last page...all the while wishing that the book was a little longer...that the ending wasn't so near...after all, an amazing story is going on...I want to keep reading it..<br /><br />By far, this has topped among the other three I've read by the madam...and though I am not very happy with the way ending was written (a little too dramatic...or maybe rushed up...or maybe I just couldn't believe people could do such stupid things)...but I was totally into it...<br /><br />Ms T has a big role in it...she is so sweet...anyone's heart would go for her...though Mommy Ryn did make me wish to slap her a few times, for so very obvious reasons...I guess one of the 'wants-to-be-dad' stole my heart...even when he did do something even more stupid than the mum..<br /><br />I can't call her novels chick lits...chicklits are by Sophie..they make u smile, they take u in a full of non sense but fun world...I don't know which category her novels fit it...I just know they always do touch your heart...<br /><br />All I could think of last night was...<br />I like Kinsellas...<br />I respect Picoult,<br />But I seriously adore Koomson...<br /><br />Way to go...a must read!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5943996651088487054">I really enjoyed this book, which I would categorize as "meaty" chick lit. The main character is flawed but entirely sympathetic and finds her heart torn between two men, both of whom are good guys but also flawed. All of this occurs in the aftermath of her being asked to adopt her dying friend's daughter, even though the two friends had not spoken for years after a falling out. The plot and characters were compelling and I was driven to finish the whole novel within 24 hours. I enjoyed the ulti</span>
  <span id="freeText5943996651088487054" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book, which I would categorize as "meaty" chick lit. The main character is flawed but entirely sympathetic and finds her heart torn between two men, both of whom are good guys but also flawed. All of this occurs in the aftermath of her being asked to adopt her dying friend's daughter, even though the two friends had not spoken for years after a falling out. The plot and characters were compelling and I was driven to finish the whole novel within 24 hours. I enjoyed the ultimate message of optimism as the book explored how people fail miserably, yet discover they are able to forgive and also redeem themselves and become something better than they were before.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347579308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2264930074442267424">This book amazed me. It was worth every minute I spent on it. Koomson tells the story of two women who are trying to adjust to their new lives together. Trough tears and laughter they find way to support each other in the most unexpected way. I love this book and I would recommend it to anyone. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5JjJ0l5UH9BSj6FteoWhcYHDex/k3svJn7PQ0knl1jyC/dHbRXtCIfIf9iyW8jZkuynXy870UPNvFhW9aDfoiA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yp/Z222AVb4YWcBCq9n3wj3Wbr6zZB4rTF0iw6c9Uoes+sHSdq8IT7jJlwNHrmDXBzzCaplOhRG8+Oeshu9sMw==')})
  }

Now in her early thirties, Melody lives in a council flat in the middle of London with her seventeen-year-old son. She hasn\'t seen her parents since she left home at fifteen, but Melody doesn\'t mind, she\'s better off on her own. She\'s made a good life for herself and her son and she likes it that way. Until one night something extraordinary happens. Whilst attending a hypnotist show with her first date in years she faints - and when she comes round she starts to remember. <span id="freeTextContainer11178832326198236765">Hello, my name's Dorothy Koomson and I'll try to make this bit that's all about me as interesting as possible.<br/>I wrote my first novel called There's A Thin Line Between Love And Hate when I was 13. I used to write a chapter every night then pass it around to my fellow convent school pupils every morning, and they seemed to love it.<br/><br/>I grew up in London and then grew up again in Leeds when I went to u</span>
  <span id="freeText11178832326198236765" style="display:none">Hello, my name's Dorothy Koomson and I'll try to make this bit that's all about me as interesting as possible.<br />I wrote my first novel called There's A Thin Line Between Love And Hate when I was 13. I used to write a chapter every night then pass it around to my fellow convent school pupils every morning, and they seemed to love it.<br /><br />I grew up in London and then grew up again in Leeds when I went to university. I eventually returned to London to study for my masters degree and stayed put for the following years. I took up various temping jobs and eventually got my big break writing, editing and subbing for various women's magazines and national papers.<br /><br />Fiction and storytelling were still a HUGE passion of mine and I continued to write short stories and novels every spare moment that I got. In 2001 I had the idea for The Cupid Effect and my career as a published novelist began. And it's been fantastic. In 2006, third novel, My Best Friend's Girl was published. It was incredibly successful - selling nearly 90,000 copies within its first few weeks on sale. Six weeks later, it was selected for the Richard &amp; Judy Summer Reads Book Club and the book went on to sell over 500,000 copies. Oh, there I go again, this is meant to be about me, not my novels.<br /><br />Okay, back to me. I recently spent two years living in Sydney Australia, and now I'm back in England. But I can't say for how long I'll be in the UK for because I've been well and truly bitten by the travel bug</span>
